{"nick":"Sorella","message":"roo_: instead, Node uses an evented model. You have only one thread of execution, so your program can only ever execute a single thing at any given time. To compose concurrent processes, Node uses asynchronous functions. Asynchronous functions are just things that start background processes, and return immediately, and then, when that process is done, it","date":"2015-09-12T23:51:50.662Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"Sorella","message":"adds an event to a queue, which is processed when there's nothing else left to process in your program. Callbacks are called by adding events to this queue. Because Node chose this model of concurrency, it had to make anything that takes more than a couple of milliseconds to execute (mainly I/O operations) an asynchronous function. And to deal with","date":"2015-09-12T23:51:50.711Z","type":"message"}
{"nick":"Sorella","message":"asynchronous functions you can only use things like promises, callbacks, or similar things","date":"2015-09-12T23:51:50.711Z","type":"message"}

{"nick":"Sorella","message":"roo_: no. Threads don't correspond to \"speed.\" In fact, Node's approach is usually faster, because I/O doesn't require computational power. You're mostly waiting.
